If the council and the firefighters union had not been able to reach agreement, the issue would have gone to the voters in November. An independent fact-finder was hired in September to settle the salary impasse. (Camera, Oct. 19, Daryl Gibson)

An American Indian filed a \$15 million lawsuit against the city claiming that police officers beat him and displayed racial prejudice against him. (Times-Call, May 4)

A Boulder man filed suit for more than \$2.4 million against the Boulder Police Department alleging police brutality during an arrest on March 11. He claims that he was incarcerated in jail for five days and was refused medical treatment. (Camera, Oct. 18, Valerie Finholm)

In December 1981, authorities found eight pounds of cocaine, 15 pounds of marijuana and drug-processing equipment in a home on Flagstaff Mountain. In 1982, the home was seized as a public nuisance. The home was sold this year for \$150,000. As a result, eight local agencies and the Denver Police Department were given part of the proceeds. Boulder Police Department's Narcotics/SCAT unit received \$23,398. (Camera, March 31, Betsy Howard)

Boulder police made what is believed to be the largest cocaine seizure in Colorado history, taking 14.2 pounds of the drug from a locker at a local athletic club. (Camera, July 9, Bruce Langer)

The city council decided not to interfere with the police chief's

decision to put two full-time police officers on duty at the Crossroads Mall. (Camera, Oct. 6, Daryl Gibson)

About 120 people responded to be tested for 10 to 12 positions open in the Boulder Police Department. (Camera, Nov. 30, Kevin O'Brien)

### FLOODS

The council unanimously approved changes to the city's flood control ordinance. One change requires motels, hotels and other "temporary" residences built or remodeled in the floodway of Boulder Creek to install warning systems in each room to warn occupants of floods. Another requires owners of rental property in the floodway to post notice on the premises that the property lies within a flood hazard area. (Camera, May 4, Sharon Gillen)

### WEATHER

An April storm, accompanied by record cold, left up to 20 inches of wet snow in west Boulder.

In May, a storm brought a covering of ice over Boulder County felling hundreds of power poles.

The temperature fell below zero on December 16 and stayed there for nearly five days, the longest stretch of sub-zero weather in 86 years of record keeping. (Camera, Jan. 4, 1984, Todd Malmsbury)

A medium-sized windstorm with gusts as high as 102 mph at the National Center for Atmospheric Research hit Boulder. (Camera, Dec. 8)

Boulder's snowstorm of November 26-27 cost the city \$143,000 to plow, haul, salt and sand. The sand which is a life-saver during the storm becomes a hazard to bicyclists once warm weather returns. If it is not

swept up after melting occurs, it will clog storm sewers later. And the salt has damaged landscaping along the streets. (Camera, Dec. 21, Daryl Gibson)

1984

### FIRE AND POLICE

~~Boulder Fire Chief Chuck Boyes is working with his counterparts in~~ neighboring communities to develop a response plan to accidents involving hazardous materials. (Camera, Feb. 5)

Last spring, the fire department began an effort to bring the CU fraternities and sororities up to fire codes, the first such thorough inspection in the city's history. All twenty-eight buildings violated life-safety codes. Major violations totaled 506. (Camera, March 4)

In the past two years, CU has spent about \$1.5 million on fire safety improvements for residence dormitories. (Colorado Daily, Sept. 19, Mark Johnson)

Six units of a three-story condominium were destroyed by a fire that left 30 people homeless. Damage was estimated at \$450,000. (Camera, Nov. 6)

After 24 years in the Boulder Fire Department, Lt. Bob Dutton has retired. (The Blaze, Vol. 3, No. 12, Dec. 1984)

The city may have "misled" firefighters in their hopes for regular increases in pension payments, but it isn't legally bound to ante up.

District Judge Morris Sandstead turned down a suit filed in 1981 by

two firefighters, two retired firefighters and the widow of a firefighter. They claimed that in exchange for increased contributions from employees to the firefighters pension fund, the Boulder City Council promised in 1973 to regularly increase pension payments by 1980. When the city did not act on the issue, the suit was filed. (Camera, June 27, Linda Cornett)

The council agreed to increase pensions paid to retired firefighters and police officers by 10.6 percent. The annual cost will be \$48,000. (Camera, Sept. 27, Linda Cornett)

Boulder firefighters approved a contract with the city that will raise their salaries almost seven percent in 1985. (Camera, Sept. 15, Kurt Chandler)

In a supplemental budget request, the police department asked for \$59,313 more to "handle the increased number of drug cases". Most of the money would be used to hire two new narcotics officers. (Camera, April 26, Brighid Kelly)

The Boulder Police Association and the city negotiated a five percent wage hike for 1985 and a five and one quarter percent increase for 1986. (Camera, Sept. 15, Kurt Chandler)

### FLOODS

Two construction projects will be allowed to go ahead because the council agreed to amend its flood control ordinance. They eliminated from the regulations a provision that made it illegal to put electrical equipment in a building below the level of a potential flood. That law would have made it impossible for the Exeter office building at 11th and Walnut streets and the proposed hotel at Ninth and Canyon Boulevard to design underground parking garages. The amendment allows exceptions to be

made if a significant financial hardship would be imposed on the developer because of the law. (Camera, Jan. 18, Daryl Gibson)

The city council approved an ordinance that would allow some residential construction in the floodways of the 12 tributaries to Boulder Creek. It provides that owners of properties along the tributaries may apply for floodway permits to build on them but only if they build two feet above the level of a major flood and if the new construction does not cause flood waters to rise. (Camera, Aug. 22, Linda Cornett)

The council agreed to create a blue ribbon panel to find ways to reduce flooding from the city's 12 tributaries. They will base their recommendations on a study prepared by the consulting firm of Greenhorne and O'Mara. (Camera, Sept. 5, Linda Cornett)

### WEATHER

The temperature plunged to 19 below zero in Boulder breaking the previous record for the date of 15 below set in 1943. The last time the official Boulder temperature was colder was on Jan. 12, 1963 when the mercury fell to 22 below. (Camera, Jan. 19, Todd Malmsbury)

A "routine" windstorm blew across Boulder with the peak gust recorded at 80 mph at NCAR. (Camera, Nov. 29, Bruce Langer and Todd Malmsbury)

Chinook winds peaked at 108 mph but only minor damage was reported. (Camera, Dec. 24, Brighid Kelly)
